          <div class="BVRRReviewDisplayStyle5Text">
           <div class="BVRRReviewTextContainer" itemprop="description">
            \n\n\n\n\n\n
            <div class="BVRRReviewText" id="BVRRReview154499698_hhx8ov4uekm72y54knvus6b3a_ID">
             <div bvrrreviewtextfirstparagraph="" bvrrreviewtextlastparagraph="" class="BVRRReviewTextParagraph">
              <span class="BVRRReviewText">
               I bought this water heater as an auxiliary unit and it looks nice enough. I had to order it
               <br/>
               since units with the 3800 watt elements are not carried in stock; yet many agencies recommend this wattage as compared to 4500 elements to save energy and still have a very good recovery cycle. My only concern is the plastic drain valve at the bottom. They tend to break/crack and leak with repeated use and should be replaced with a brass drain valve. Most plumbers recommend draining and flushing the water heater annually so this plastic drain valve is an issue.
              </span>
              \n
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           \n

            In reading your review, it is apparent you had just purchased a Rheem NAECA III rated water heater and are concerned that the Federal estimated annual operating costs are higher than your older State water heater.
            <br/>
            I appreciated your concerns and on the surface you would think that with a higher energy efficiency standard the costs would be lower. Which in reality they probably are.
            <br/>
            I do not have the information of your previous State water heater nor the exact current model number of your unit to compare with.
            <br/>
            None the less there are several factors that the government puts into this annual estimate. First of which is the \u201cAverage Daily Usage\u201d which may have gone up since you purchased your State water heater. The next and critical factor is the \u201cCost of Energy\u201d which may have gone up since you purchased your State water heater.
            <br/>
            Below is the government web site to assist in estimating your annual costs per your specific factors.

             <div bvrrreviewtextfirstparagraph="" bvrrreviewtextlastparagraph="" class="BVRRReviewTextParagraph">
              <span class="BVRRReviewText">
               Installed it myself. When I primed the tank I noticed a leak down at the drain pipe. The valve was closed it was the pipe itself leaking from in side. After about 3-5 turns with my pipe wrench the problem stopped. I would suggest the drain pipe be tightened appropriately at the manufacturer and test for leaks before distribution.
